<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en"><i>Ace Attorney</i></h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>

<p><i><b>Ace Attorney</b></i>, known in Japan as <i><b>Gyakuten Saiban</b></i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a>: <span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja" xml:lang="ja">逆転裁判</span><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>, "Turnabout Trial")</span>, is a series of <a href="/wiki/Visual_novel" title="Visual novel">visual novel</a> <a href="/wiki/Adventure_game" title="Adventure game">adventure video games</a> developed by <a href="/wiki/Capcom" title="Capcom">Capcom</a>. The first entry in the series, <i><a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Wright:_Ace_Attorney" title="Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney">Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney</a></i>, was released in 2001; since then, nine further games have been released. Additionally, the series has seen adaptations in the form of <a href="/wiki/Ace_Attorney_(film)" title="Ace Attorney (film)">a live action film</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ace_Attorney_(anime)" title="Ace Attorney (anime)">an anime</a>, and has been the base for <a href="/wiki/Manga" title="Manga">manga</a> series, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drama_CD" title="Drama CD">drama CDs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Musical_theatre" title="Musical theatre">musicals</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stage_play" title="Stage play">stage plays</a>.</p>
<p>The player takes the roles of the defense attorneys <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Wright_(character)" title="Phoenix Wright (character)">Phoenix Wright</a>, Mia Fey, Apollo Justice and Athena Cykes, and investigates cases and defends their clients in court; they find the truth by cross-examining witnesses and finding inconsistencies between the testimonies and the evidence they have collected. The cases all last a maximum of three days, with the judge determining the outcome based on evidence presented by the defense attorney and the prosecutor. In the spin-off series <i>Ace Attorney Investigations</i>, the player takes the role of prosecutor <a href="/wiki/Miles_Edgeworth" title="Miles Edgeworth">Miles Edgeworth</a>, and in the spin-off <i><a href="/wiki/Dai_Gyakuten_Saiban:_Naruhod%C5%8D_Ry%C5%ABnosuke_no_B%C5%8Dken" title="Dai Gyakuten Saiban: Naruhodō Ryūnosuke no Bōken">Dai Gyakuten Saiban</a></i>, they play as Phoenix's ancestor Ryūnosuke Naruhodō.</p>
<p>The series was created by the writer and director <a href="/wiki/Shu_Takumi" title="Shu Takumi">Shu Takumi</a>, who wanted the series to end after the third game. The series still continued, with Takeshi Yamazaki taking over as writer and director starting with <i><a href="/wiki/Ace_Attorney_Investigations:_Miles_Edgeworth" title="Ace Attorney Investigations: Miles Edgeworth">Ace Attorney Investigations: Miles Edgeworth</a></i> (2009); Takumi has since returned to write and direct some spin-off titles. While the original Japanese versions of the games are set in Japan, the series' <a href="/wiki/Video_game_localization" title="Video game localization">localizations</a> are set in the United States, though retaining Japanese cultural influence. The series has been well received, with reviewers liking the characters and story, and the finding of contradictions; it has also performed well commercially, with Capcom regarding it as one of their strongest intellectual properties.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles">Titles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ace_Attorney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Titles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <i>Ace Attorney</i> series launched in Japan with the <a href="/wiki/Game_Boy_Advance" title="Game Boy Advance">Game Boy Advance</a> game <i><a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Wright:_Ace_Attorney" title="Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney">Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney</a></i> in 2001, and has been published in the West since the release of a <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_DS" title="Nintendo DS">Nintendo DS</a> port in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann_anime_staff_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-ann_anime_staff-3">[3]</a></sup> The series currently consists of six main series games and four spin-offs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sil_aa6_3ds_ja_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-sil_aa6_3ds_ja-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_dgs1_3ds_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_dgs1_3ds-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aai1_nds_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aai1_nds-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aai2_nds_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aai2_nds-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_plvsaa_3ds_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_plvsaa_3ds-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sil_aa6_3ds_naeu_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-sil_aa6_3ds_naeu-8">[8]</a></sup> Additionally, two titles that collect the first three main series games have been released: <i>Ace Attorney: Phoenix Wright Trilogy HD</i>, which was released for iOS and Android in 2012 in Japan and for iOS in 2013 in the West,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_tri_ios_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_tri_ios-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kot_tri_ios_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-kot_tri_ios-11">[11]</a></sup> and <i>Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney Trilogy</i>, which was released for the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_3DS" title="Nintendo 3DS">Nintendo 3DS</a> in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_tri_3ds_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_tri_3ds-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pol_tri_3ds_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-pol_tri_3ds-13">[13]</a></sup></p>

<td scope="row" style="text-align:right;border:none;padding:5px;border-right:16px solid #0BDA51">TBA</td>
<td style="padding:5px;border:none"><i>Dai Gyakuten Saiban 2: Naruhodō Ryūnosuke no Kakugo</i></td>

</table>
<ul>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Wright:_Ace_Attorney" title="Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney">Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney</a></b></i> is the first entry in the series. It was originally released for the Game Boy Advance in 2001 in Japan;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aa1_gba_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aa1_gba-1">[1]</a></sup> it has also been released for the Nintendo DS in 2005,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aa1_nds_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aa1_nds-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> in 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1up_pc_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-1up_pc-15">[15]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a> and <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aa1_wii_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aa1_wii-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aa1_ios_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aa1_ios-17">[17]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Wright:_Ace_Attorney_%E2%88%92_Justice_for_All" title="Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney − Justice for All">Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney − Justice for All</a></b></i> is the second entry in the series. It was originally released for the Game Boy Advance in 2002 in Japan;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aa2_gba_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aa2_gba-18">[18]</a></sup> it has also been released for the Nintendo DS in 2006,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aa2_nds_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aa2_nds-19">[19]</a></sup> Microsoft Windows in 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1up_pc_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-1up_pc-15">[15]</a></sup> and the Wii in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aa2_wii_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aa2_wii-20">[20]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Wright:_Ace_Attorney_%E2%88%92_Trials_and_Tribulations" title="Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney − Trials and Tribulations">Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney − Trials and Tribulations</a></b></i> is the third entry in the series. It was originally released for the Game Boy Advance in 2004 in Japan;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aa3_gba_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aa3_gba-21">[21]</a></sup> it has also been released for Microsoft Windows in 2006,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4g_aa3_win_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-4g_aa3_win-22">[22]</a></sup> the Nintendo DS in 2007,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aa3_nds_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aa3_nds-23">[23]</a></sup> and the Wii in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aa3_wii_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aa3_wii-24">[24]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Apollo_Justice:_Ace_Attorney" title="Apollo Justice: Ace Attorney">Apollo Justice: Ace Attorney</a></b></i> is the fourth entry in the series. It was released for the Nintendo DS in 2007 in Japan<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aa4_nds_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aa4_nds-25">[25]</a></sup> and in 2008 in the West,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cap_aa4_nds_na_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-cap_aa4_nds_na-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nin_aa4_nds_eu_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-nin_aa4_nds_eu-27">[27]</a></sup> and for iOS and Android in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Wright:_Ace_Attorney_%E2%88%92_Dual_Destinies" title="Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney − Dual Destinies">Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney − Dual Destinies</a></b></i> is the fifth entry in the main series. It was originally released for the Nintendo 3DS in 2013 in Japan, North America and Europe; outside of Japan, it was given a digital-only release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aa5_3ds_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aa5_3ds-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pol_aa5_digital_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-pol_aa5_digital-31">[31]</a></sup> An iOS version was released in 2014 in Japan and the West.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aa5_ios_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aa5_ios-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-destruct_aa5_ios_eng_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-destruct_aa5_ios_eng-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Wright:_Ace_Attorney_%E2%88%92_Spirit_of_Justice" title="Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney − Spirit of Justice">Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney − Spirit of Justice</a></b></i> is the sixth entry in the main series. It was released for the Nintendo 3DS in 2016 in Japan, North America and Europe. Like <i>Dual Destinies</i>, it was given a digital-only release outside Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sil_aa6_3ds_ja_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-sil_aa6_3ds_ja-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sil_aa6_3ds_naeu_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-sil_aa6_3ds_naeu-8">[8]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spin-offs">Spin-offs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ace_Attorney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Spin-offs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Ace_Attorney_Investigations:_Miles_Edgeworth" title="Ace Attorney Investigations: Miles Edgeworth">Ace Attorney Investigations: Miles Edgeworth</a></b></i> is the first entry in the <i>Investigations</i> spin-off series. It was released for the Nintendo DS in 2009 in Japan<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aai1_nds_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aai1_nds-5">[5]</a></sup> and in 2010 in the West.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Ace_Attorney_Investigations_2" title="Ace Attorney Investigations 2">Ace Attorney Investigations 2</a></b></i> is the second entry in the <i>Investigations</i> series. It was released for the Nintendo DS in 2011 in Japan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aai2_nds_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aai2_nds-6">[6]</a></sup> but has not been released in the West.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usg_aai2_limbo_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-usg_aai2_limbo-35">[35]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Professor_Layton_vs._Phoenix_Wright:_Ace_Attorney" title="Professor Layton vs. Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney">Professor Layton vs. Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney</a></b></i> is a <a href="/wiki/Crossovers_in_video_games" title="Crossovers in video games">crossover</a> between <i>Ace Attorney</i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Professor_Layton" title="Professor Layton">Professor Layton</a></i> series. It was released for the Nintendo 3DS in 2012 in Japan<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_plvsaa_3ds_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-fam_plvsaa_3ds-7">[7]</a></sup> and in 2014 in the West.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pol_plvsaa_3ds_naeu_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-pol_plvsaa_3ds_naeu-36">[36]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Dai_Gyakuten_Saiban:_Naruhod%C5%8D_Ry%C5%ABnosuke_no_B%C5%8Dken" title="Dai Gyakuten Saiban: Naruhodō Ryūnosuke no Bōken">Dai Gyakuten Saiban: Naruhodō Ryūnosuke no Bōken</a></b></i> is the first entry in the <i>Dai Gyakuten Saiban</i> spin-off series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sil_dgs_new_series_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-sil_dgs_new_series-37">[37]</a></sup> It was released for the Nintendo 3DS in 2015 in Japan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_dgs1_3ds_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-fam_dgs1_3ds-4">[4]</a></sup> but is not intended to be released in the West.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dgs_capcom_france_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-dgs_capcom_france-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><b>Dai Gyakuten Saiban 2: Naruhodō Ryūnosuke no Kakugo</b></i> is the upcoming second entry in the <i>Dai Gyakuten Saiban</i> series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> It is planned to be released for the Nintendo 3DS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Common_elements">Common elements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ace_Attorney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Common elements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gameplay">Gameplay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ace_Attorney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Gameplay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phoenix_Wright_Ace_Attorney_cross-examination.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="384" data-file-width="256" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5d/Phoenix_Wright_Ace_Attorney_cross-examination.png/220px-Phoenix_Wright_Ace_Attorney_cross-examination.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/5d/Phoenix_Wright_Ace_Attorney_cross-examination.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Phoenix_Wright_Ace_Attorney_cross-examination.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A cross-examination in the first game, with the witness on the top screen. The player can move between statements, press the witness for details, and show evidence that contradicts the testimony.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i>Ace Attorney</i> games are <a href="/wiki/Visual_novel" title="Visual novel">visual novel</a> <a href="/wiki/Adventure_game" title="Adventure game">adventure games</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toucharcade_aa5_ios_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-toucharcade_aa5_ios-41">[41]</a></sup> in which the player controls <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Defense_attorney" title="Defense attorney">defense attorneys</a> and defends their clients in several different episodes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aa2_gspot_rev_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-aa2_gspot_rev-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aa3_nwr_rev_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-aa3_nwr_rev-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The gameplay is split into two types of sections: investigations and courtroom trials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwr_rev_ds_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-nwr_rev_ds-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> During the investigations, the player searches the environments, gathering information and evidence, and talks to characters such as their client, witnesses, and the police.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwr_rev_ds_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-nwr_rev_ds-45">[45]</a></sup> Once enough evidence has been collected, the game moves on to a courtroom trial section.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the courtroom trials, the player aims to get their client declared "not guilty". To do so, they cross-examine witnesses,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwr_rev_ds_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-nwr_rev_ds-45">[45]</a></sup> and aim to find lies and inconsistencies in the testimonies. They are able to go back and forth between the different statements in the testimony, and can press the witness for more details on a statement. When the player finds an inconsistency, they can present a piece of evidence that contradicts the statement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The player is penalized if they present incorrect evidence: in the first game, a number of exclamation marks is shown, with one disappearing after each mistake the player makes;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pw_manual_p20_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-pw_manual_p20-51">[51]</a></sup> in later games, a health bar that represents the judge's patience is used instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jfa_manual_pg20-21_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-jfa_manual_pg20-21-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aj_manual_p22_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-aj_manual_p22-54">[54]</a></sup> If all exclamation marks are lost, or the health bar reaches zero, the player loses the game and their client is declared guilty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pw_manual_p20_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-pw_manual_p20-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jfa_manual_pg20-21_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-jfa_manual_pg20-21-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aj_manual_p22_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-aj_manual_p22-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several <i>Ace Attorney</i> games introduce new gameplay mechanics to the series. <i>Justice for All</i> introduces "psyche-locks", which are shown over a witness when the player asks them about a topic they do not want to discuss; using a <i><a href="/wiki/Magatama" title="Magatama">magatama</a></i>, the player can start breaking the psyche-locks by showing the witness evidence or character profiles that proves they are hiding something. The number of psyche-locks depends on how deep the secret is; when all locks are broken, the topic becomes available, giving the player access to new information.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aa2_eurogamer_rev_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-aa2_eurogamer_rev-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> <i>Apollo Justice</i> introduces the "perceive" system, where the player looks for motions or actions made by witnesses that show nervousness, similar to a <a href="/wiki/Tell_(poker)" title="Tell (poker)">tell in poker</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Dual Destinies</i> introduces the "mood matrix", through which the player can gauge the emotions of a witness, such as tones of anger when mentioning certain topics;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> if the player notices a contradictory emotional response during testimony, they can point out the discrepancy and press the witness for more information.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> <i>Dual Destinies</i> also introduces "revisualization",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TR_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-TR-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> where the player reviews vital facts and forms links between evidence to reach new conclusions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TR_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-TR-61">[61]</a></sup> <i>Spirit of Justice</i> introduces "divination <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9ance" title="Séance">séances</a>", in which the player is shown the memories of victims moments before their deaths, and must find contradictions in the victim's five senses to determine what has happened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spiritvision_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-spiritvision-63">[63]</a></sup> <i>Professor Layton vs. Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney</i> introduces simultaneous cross-examinations of multiple witnesses, with the player being able to see and hear reactions from the different witnesses to the testimony and using this to find contradictions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> <i>Dai Gyakuten Saiban</i> introduces "joint reasoning", where the player finds out the truth by pointing out when their investigative partner <a href="/wiki/Sherlock_Holmes" title="Sherlock Holmes">Sherlock Holmes</a> takes his reasoning "further than the truth".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Ace Attorney Investigations</i> spin-off series splits the gameplay into investigation phases and rebuttal phases, the latter of which is similar to the courtroom trials of the main series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aai_nwr_rev_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-aai_nwr_rev-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aai2_jeuxvideo_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-aai2_jeuxvideo-68">[68]</a></sup> During the investigation phases, the player searches for evidence and talks to witnesses and suspects. Things the player character notices in the environment are saved as thoughts; the player can use the "logic" system to connect two such thoughts to gain access to new information.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aai_nwr_rev_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-aai_nwr_rev-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aai_gspot_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-aai_gspot-69">[69]</a></sup> At some points, the player can create <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hologram" title="Hologram">hologram</a> reproductions of the crime scene,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aai_nwr_rev_66-2"><a href="#cite_note-aai_nwr_rev-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aai_eurog_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-aai_eurog-70">[70]</a></sup> through which they can discover new information that would otherwise be hidden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> <i>Ace Attorney Investigations 2</i> introduces "logic chess", where the player interrogates witnesses in a timed sequence that is visualized as a game of chess, with the player aiming to destroy the other character's chess pieces. To do this, they need to build up their advantage in the discussion by alternating between speaking and listening, and then choose to go on the offensive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aai2_jeuxvideo_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-aai2_jeuxvideo-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aai2_chess_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-aai2_chess-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nf_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-nf-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Characters_and_setting">Characters and setting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ace_Attorney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Characters and setting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ace_Attorney_characters" title="List of Ace Attorney characters">List of Ace Attorney characters</a></div>
<p>The protagonist of the first three games is the defense attorney <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Wright_(character)" title="Phoenix Wright (character)">Phoenix Wright</a>, who is assisted by the spirit medium Maya Fey;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hardcore_trilogy_rev_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-hardcore_trilogy_rev-74">[74]</a></sup> in the third game, Phoenix's mentor Mia Fey is also a playable character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aa3_nwr_rev_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-aa3_nwr_rev-43">[43]</a></sup> In the fourth game, the protagonist is the defense attorney Apollo Justice;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> in the fifth, Phoenix, Apollo and the new defense attorney Athena Cykes are all protagonists;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> and in the sixth, Phoenix and Apollo are the protagonists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The spin-off <i>Dai Gyakuten Saiban</i> is set in England near the end of the 19th century, and follows Phoenix's ancestor Ryūnosuke Naruhodō.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Phoenix's childhood friend <a href="/wiki/Miles_Edgeworth" title="Miles Edgeworth">Miles Edgeworth</a>, who is the protagonist of the <i>Ace Attorney Investigations</i> games,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aai_nwr_rev_66-3"><a href="#cite_note-aai_nwr_rev-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aai2_jeuxvideo_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-aai2_jeuxvideo-68">[68]</a></sup> is a recurring rival prosecutor character; in addition to him, each new game in the series introduces a new rival:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hardcore_trilogy_rev_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-hardcore_trilogy_rev-74">[74]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Franziska_von_Karma" title="Franziska von Karma">Franziska von Karma</a> is introduced in the second game,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-capcom-unity_tidbits_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-capcom-unity_tidbits-79">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Godot_(Ace_Attorney)" title="Godot (Ace Attorney)">Godot</a> in the third,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Klavier Gavin in the fourth,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Simon Blackquill in the fifth,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> and Nahyuta Sahdmadhi in the sixth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The prosecutor characters are portrayed as powerful and arrogant characters of high social status, who favor convictions over finding the truth, and who care about keeping perfect-win records in court. Similarly to real Japanese prosecutors, the prosecutors in the series often directly oversee investigations, issuing orders to the police. Japanese attitudes towards the police force are reflected in the series, with the police being represented by incompetent characters such as Dick Gumshoe, Maggey Byrde and Mike Meekins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-escapist_japanese_courts_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-escapist_japanese_courts-84">[84]</a></sup> In the world of <i>Ace Attorney</i>, trials only last three days, and usually end with a "guilty" verdict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hardcore_trilogy_rev_74-2"><a href="#cite_note-hardcore_trilogy_rev-74">[74]</a></sup> The outcomes of cases are decided by a judge, based on evidence provided by the defense attorney and the prosecutor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-escapist_japanese_courts_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-escapist_japanese_courts-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ace_Attorney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ghost_Trick_event_4_-_cropped.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2924" data-file-width="1979" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Ghost_Trick_event_4_-_cropped.jpg/170px-Ghost_Trick_event_4_-_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Ghost_Trick_event_4_-_cropped.jpg/255px-Ghost_Trick_event_4_-_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Ghost_Trick_event_4_-_cropped.jpg/340px-Ghost_Trick_event_4_-_cropped.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ghost_Trick_event_4_-_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The series was created by <a href="/wiki/Shu_Takumi" title="Shu Takumi">Shu Takumi</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The series was created by <a href="/wiki/Shu_Takumi" title="Shu Takumi">Shu Takumi</a>, who wrote and directed the first three games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> The first game was conceived in 2000 when Takumi's boss at the time, <a href="/wiki/Shinji_Mikami" title="Shinji Mikami">Shinji Mikami</a>, gave him six months to create any type of game he wanted to; Takumi had originally joined Capcom wanting to make mystery and adventure games, and felt that this was a big chance for him to make a mark as a creator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onm_making_of_pg1_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-onm_making_of_pg1-86">[86]</a></sup> The game was designed to be simple, as Takumi wanted it to be easy enough for even his mother to play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-capcom-unity_tidbits_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-capcom-unity_tidbits-79">[79]</a></sup> It was originally going to be a detective game, with Phoenix being a <a href="/wiki/Private_investigator" title="Private investigator">private investigator</a>, but at one point Takumi realized that finding and taking apart contradictions was not related to detective work, and felt that the main setting of the game should be courtrooms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-capcom-unity_early_days_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-capcom-unity_early_days-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>Takumi felt that the best way to write a mystery with a good climax is to reveal various clues, and then pull them together into one conclusion, and not have multiple possible endings. He said that the biggest challenge with that was to make the gameplay and story work together; the goal was to make the player feel like they have driven the story forward themselves, with their own choices, even though the game is linear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onm_trilogy_pg1_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-onm_trilogy_pg1-88">[88]</a></sup> He only spent little time on writing a backstory for Phoenix before writing the first game's story, and instead made up dialogue and developed Phoenix's personality as he went along.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onm_trilogy_pg1_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-onm_trilogy_pg1-88">[88]</a></sup> He came up with the partner character Maya because he thought it would be more fun for players to have another character with them, giving them advice, than investigating on their own.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onm_trilogy_pg1_88-2"><a href="#cite_note-onm_trilogy_pg1-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the first game's development was finished, Mikami told Takumi that they should make an <i>Ace Attorney</i> trilogy, with a grand finale in the third game's last case.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onm_trilogy_pg3_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-onm_trilogy_pg3-89">[89]</a></sup> Takumi had originally planned to let Edgeworth be the prosecutor in all episodes in the second game,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onm_trilogy_pg2_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-onm_trilogy_pg2-90">[90]</a></sup> but during the production the development team learned that the character had become popular. This led to Takumi feeling that he had to use the character more carefully and sparingly; he created the new prosecutor character Franziska von Karma, to save Edgeworth for the game's last case, and avoid a situation where he – a supposed prodigy – loses every case.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-capcom-unity_tidbits_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-capcom-unity_tidbits-79">[79]</a></sup> As Takumi wanted the three first <i>Ace Attorney</i> games to be parts of a larger work, he avoided making a lot of changes between games: art from the first game for main characters such as Phoenix, Maya and Edgeworth was reused, to avoid having the previous games look outdated in comparison to newer games in the series; and no new gameplay mechanics were added for <i>Trials and Tribulations</i>, as Takumi was happy with the gameplay after having added the psyche-lock mechanic for <i>Justice for All</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onm_trilogy_pg2_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-onm_trilogy_pg2-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>For the fourth game, Takumi wrote the scenario and took on a supervisory role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toucharcade_aa5_ios_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-toucharcade_aa5_ios-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> He had wanted the series to end with the third game, as he felt Phoenix had been fully explored and that his story had been told; he said that it is important to know when to end a story, that he did not want the series to become a shadow of its former self, and that he did not see any reason to continue it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Despite this, the spin-off series <i>Ace Attorney Investigations</i> was created, being directed by Takeshi Yamazaki and produced by Motohide Eshiro;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Takumi returned to the series to write the crossover <i>Professor Layton vs. Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onm_making_of_pg3_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-onm_making_of_pg3-95">[95]</a></sup> He also directed and wrote <i>Dai Gyakuten Saiban</i>, which was described as being the first entry in a new <i>Ace Attorney</i> series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sil_dgs_new_series_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-sil_dgs_new_series-37">[37]</a></sup> He said that he has mixed feelings about the series being developed by other Capcom staff, comparing it to a parent sending their child to their first day in school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onm_making_of_pg4_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-onm_making_of_pg4-96">[96]</a></sup> Yamazaki and Eshiro went on to direct and produce the main series entries <i>Dual Destinies</i> and <i>Spirit of Justice</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nindori_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-nindori-99">[99]</a></sup> Due to exhaustion after working on <i>Dual Destinies</i>, Yamazaki split direction responsibilities with Takuro Fuse for <i>Spirit of Justice</i>, with Yamazaki working on the scenario, and Fuse on the art and gameplay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nindori_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-nindori-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Localization">Localization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ace_Attorney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Localization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Video_game_localization" title="Video game localization">localization</a> of the first game was outsourced to Bowne Global, and was handled by the writer <a href="/wiki/Alexander_O._Smith" title="Alexander O. Smith">Alexander O. Smith</a> and the editor Steve Anderson. While the Japanese version takes place in Japan, the localized version is set in the United States: because one of the episodes involves time zones, they had to specify where the game takes place, and chose the United States without thinking a lot about it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usgamer_alex_smith_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-usgamer_alex_smith-100">[100]</a></sup> The Japanese justice system of the original still remained intact in the localization, as changing it would have altered the entire game structure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nintendo_wright_track_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-nintendo_wright_track-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>The change in the series' setting became an issue in later games, where the Japanese setting was more obvious.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usgamer_alex_smith_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-usgamer_alex_smith-100">[100]</a></sup> Starting with the second game, the series localization direction has been handled by Janet Hsu;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-capcom-unity_tidbits_79-3"><a href="#cite_note-capcom-unity_tidbits-79">[79]</a></sup> One of the first decisions she had to make was how to localize Maya's hometown and the mysticism of the Fey clan. She came up with the idea that the localized versions of the <i>Ace Attorney</i> games take place in Los Angeles in an alternative universe where anti-Japanese laws like the <a href="/wiki/California_Alien_Land_Law_of_1913" title="California Alien Land Law of 1913">California Alien Land Law of 1913</a> were not passed, anti-Japanese sentiments were not powerful, and where Japanese culture flourished. This dictated what should be localized and what should be kept Japanese; things relating to the Fey clan and the Kurain channeling technique were kept Japanese, as that was Maya's heritage, while Japanese foods that were not widely known in the West were changed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-capcom-unity_tidbits_79-4"><a href="#cite_note-capcom-unity_tidbits-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-capcom-unity_localization_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-capcom-unity_localization-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>Character names were also localized to use double meanings similarly to the Japanese names;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nintendo_wright_track_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-nintendo_wright_track-101">[101]</a></sup> the name puns were based on the characters' personalities or backgrounds, or were visual gags.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sil_lawyers_localization_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-sil_lawyers_localization-103">[103]</a></sup> Several English names were based on their Japanese counterparts, but for some characters the names had to be altered heavily compared to the Japanese versions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nintendo_wright_track_101-2"><a href="#cite_note-nintendo_wright_track-101">[101]</a></sup> Smith and Anderson had a lot of freedom when localizing the names of minor characters in the first game, but discussed the names of the main cast with Capcom. Phoenix's English surname, "Wright", was chosen as his Japanese name, "Naruhodō" – meaning "I see" or "I understand" – was frequently used as a joke in the script.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usgamer_alex_smith_100-2"><a href="#cite_note-usgamer_alex_smith-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Dual Destinies</i> was given a digital-only release in the West. This was partially because of the game's tight development schedule: by releasing it digitally, Capcom was able to release the English version close to the Japanese release date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pol_aa5_digital_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-pol_aa5_digital-31">[31]</a></sup> Two of the games have not been localized: <i>Ace Attorney Investigations 2</i> and <i>Dai Gyakuten Saiban</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usg_aai2_limbo_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-usg_aai2_limbo-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dgs_capcom_france_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-dgs_capcom_france-38">[38]</a></sup> although the former has received a full <a href="/wiki/Fan_translation_of_video_games" title="Fan translation of video games">fan translation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usg_aai2_limbo_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-usg_aai2_limbo-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ace_Attorney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>The <i>Ace Attorney</i> series has been well received by critics,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mc_aa1_nds_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-mc_aa1_nds-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mc_aa2_nds_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-mc_aa2_nds-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mc_aa3_nds_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-mc_aa3_nds-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mc_aa4_nds_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-mc_aa4_nds-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mc_aa5_3ds_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-mc_aa5_3ds-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mc_aa6_3ds_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-mc_aa6_3ds-112">[112]</a></sup> and has performed well commercially: in December 2009, it was Capcom's 9th best selling series of all time,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> and in October 2010, they called it one of their "strongest intellectual properties", with more than 3.9 million units sold worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> By December 2013, the series had sold over 5 million units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> In the United States, the first game became surprisingly successful, forcing Capcom to prepare at least three additional runs to meet the demand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>Reviewers have liked finding contradictions;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aa1_gba_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aa1_gba-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aai_advgamers_rev_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-aai_advgamers_rev-117">[117]</a></sup> a common complaint, however, is the games' linearity,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aa2_gspot_rev_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-aa2_gspot_rev-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aa2_ign_rev_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-aa2_ign_rev-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aa3_ign_rev_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-aa3_ign_rev-119">[119]</a></sup> as well as how the player sometimes has to resort to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trial-and-error" title="Trial-and-error">trial-and-error</a> method due to the games only accepting specific pieces of evidence, and how testimony statements sometimes need to be pressed in a specific order.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aa3_nwr_rev_43-2"><a href="#cite_note-aa3_nwr_rev-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aa2_eurogamer_rev_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-aa2_eurogamer_rev-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aai_advgamers_rev_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-aai_advgamers_rev-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aa3_1up_rev_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-aa3_1up_rev-120">[120]</a></sup> Some reviewers have criticized the lack of changes to the gameplay and presentation throughout the series,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fam_aa2_gba_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-fam_aa2_gba-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aai_nwr_rev_66-4"><a href="#cite_note-aai_nwr_rev-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aa3_ign_rev_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-aa3_ign_rev-119">[119]</a></sup> while some have said that fans of the series would not have a problem with this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aai2_jeuxvideo_68-3"><a href="#cite_note-aai2_jeuxvideo-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aa3_ign_rev_119-2"><a href="#cite_note-aa3_ign_rev-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>Geoff Thew at <i><a href="/wiki/Hardcore_Gamer" title="Hardcore Gamer">Hardcore Gamer</a></i> said that the "craziness" of the game world makes the cases entertaining, but also that it "resonates on a deeper level" due to its connection to the real Japanese legal system, making the setting still feel relevant in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hardcore_trilogy_rev_74-3"><a href="#cite_note-hardcore_trilogy_rev-74">[74]</a></sup> Bob Mackey at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USgamer" title="USgamer">USgamer</a> said that the <i>Ace Attorney</i> games were among the best written games of all time, and that the series' strength is how each game builds up to a "stunning and satisfying finale".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usg_rev_3ds_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-usg_rev_3ds-121">[121]</a></sup> Thomas Whitehead at Nintendo Life also liked the writing, praising its balance between "light-hearted nonsense" and darker, more serious scenarios.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nintendo_life_rev_3ds_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-nintendo_life_rev_3ds-122">[122]</a></sup> Several reviewers have appreciated the series' characters;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aai2_jeuxvideo_68-4"><a href="#cite_note-aai2_jeuxvideo-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hardcore_trilogy_rev_74-4"><a href="#cite_note-hardcore_trilogy_rev-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usg_rev_3ds_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-usg_rev_3ds-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Thew said that Phoenix and Maya's banter is among the best in video games, and that Edgeworth's <a href="/wiki/Character_arc" title="Character arc">character arc</a> is one of the most compelling parts of the stories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hardcore_trilogy_rev_74-5"><a href="#cite_note-hardcore_trilogy_rev-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several reviewers have praised the series' music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hardcore_trilogy_rev_74-6"><a href="#cite_note-hardcore_trilogy_rev-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usg_rev_3ds_121-2"><a href="#cite_note-usg_rev_3ds-121">[121]</a></sup> Thew said that the greatest aspect of the series is its audio design, with the first three games using the Game Boy Advance sound chip better than any other game for that platform; he called the music phenomenal, with the exception of that in <i>Justice for All</i>, but said the sound effects are what "steals the show".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hardcore_trilogy_rev_74-7"><a href="#cite_note-hardcore_trilogy_rev-74">[74]</a></sup> Mackey commented that the games' small amounts of animations for each character are used well for their characterization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usg_rev_3ds_121-3"><a href="#cite_note-usg_rev_3ds-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_media_and_other_appearances">Related media and other appearances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ace_Attorney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Related media and other appearances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ace_Attorney_media" title="List of Ace Attorney media">List of Ace Attorney media</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Takarazuka_grand_theater03s3200.jpg"><img alt="A photo of the Takarauka Grand Theater." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2133" data-file-width="3200" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Takarazuka_grand_theater03s3200.jpg/220px-Takarazuka_grand_theater03s3200.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Takarazuka_grand_theater03s3200.jpg/330px-Takarazuka_grand_theater03s3200.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Takarazuka_grand_theater03s3200.jpg/440px-Takarazuka_grand_theater03s3200.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Takarazuka_grand_theater03s3200.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Takarazuka_Grand_Theater" title="Takarazuka Grand Theater">Takarazuka Grand Theater</a>. The all-female <a href="/wiki/Takarazuka_Revue" title="Takarazuka Revue">Takarazuka theater troupe</a> adapted the series into musicals.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Takarazuka_Revue" title="Takarazuka Revue">Takarazuka Revue</a>, an all-female theater troupe, has adapted the series into stage musicals: 2009's <i>Ace Attorney: Truth Resurrected</i>, which is based on the last episode of the first game;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> 2010's <i>Ace Attorney 2: Truth Resurrected Again</i>, whose first act is an original story, while its second act is based on the final episode of the second game;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> and 2013's <i>Ace Attorney 3: Prosecutor Miles Edgeworth</i>, which is set before the events of <i>Truth Resurrected Again</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stage_play" title="Stage play">stage play</a> based on the series, titled <i>Gyakuten no Spotlight</i>, ran in 2013, and was written by Eisaku Saito.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> A 2012 live-action film adaptation of the first game, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Ace_Attorney_(film)" title="Ace Attorney (film)">Ace Attorney</a></i>, was produced at the film studio <a href="/wiki/Toei_Company" title="Toei Company">Toei</a> and directed by <a href="/wiki/Takashi_Miike" title="Takashi Miike">Takashi Miike</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> A 2016 TV anime adaptation of the series, <i><a href="/wiki/Ace_Attorney_(anime)" title="Ace Attorney (anime)">Ace Attorney</a></i>, was produced at <a href="/wiki/A-1_Pictures" title="A-1 Pictures">A-1 Pictures</a> and directed by Ayumu Watanabe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ann_anime_staff_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-ann_anime_staff-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kodansha" title="Kodansha">Kodansha</a> has published several <a href="/wiki/Manga" title="Manga">manga</a> based on the series: a short story anthology was published in <i>Bessatsu Young Magazine</i> in 2006; <i>Phoenix Wright: Ace Attorney</i> and <i>Ace Attorney Investigations: Miles Edgeworth</i> were serialized in <i>Weekly Young Magazine</i> in 2007 and 2009, respectively; and another manga, which is based on the anime, will be published in <i><a href="/wiki/V_Jump" title="V Jump">V Jump</a></i> in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> A novel based on the series, <i>Gyakuten Saiban: Turnabout Idol</i>, was released in June 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> <i>Ace Attorney</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drama_CD" title="Drama CD">drama CDs</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Discography_of_the_Ace_Attorney_series" title="Discography of the Ace Attorney series"><i>Ace Attorney</i> music albums</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> and <i>Ace Attorney</i> figurines have also been released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Ace Attorney</i> characters have made cross-over appearances in other video games. Some <i>Ace Attorney</i> characters appear in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SNK_vs._Capcom_Card_Fighters_DS" title="SNK vs. Capcom Card Fighters DS">SNK vs. Capcom: Card Fighters DS</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Phoenix and Edgeworth make a cameo appearance in <a href="/wiki/She-Hulk" title="She-Hulk">She-Hulk</a>'s ending in the fighting game <i><a href="/wiki/Marvel_vs._Capcom_3:_Fate_of_Two_Worlds" title="Marvel vs. Capcom 3: Fate of Two Worlds">Marvel vs. Capcom 3: Fate of Two Worlds</a></i>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> in the game's update, <i><a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Marvel_vs._Capcom_3" title="Ultimate Marvel vs. Capcom 3">Ultimate Marvel vs. Capcom 3</a></i>, Phoenix appears as a playable character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Phoenix and Maya are playable characters in <i><a href="/wiki/Project_X_Zone_2" title="Project X Zone 2">Project X Zone 2</a></i>, while Edgeworth makes a non-playable appearance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> Phoenix, Maya, Edgeworth and Franziska were all playable in the mobile game <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monster_Hunter_Explore" title="Monster Hunter Explore">Monster Hunter Explore</a></i> in 2017, as part of one of its temporary crossover events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> Music from the <i>Ace Attorney</i> series is featured in <i><a href="/wiki/Taiko_no_Tatsujin" title="Taiko no Tatsujin">Taiko Drum Master: Doko Don! Mystery Adventure</a></i>, with Phoenix making an appearance in the game's story.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
